Supplement to the Shanghai Edition of Shen Bao

Talk

"Blacks and Chinese" 222

— Simu

According to a Reuters dispatch from Berlin on December 16, the Chinese Ambassador to Germany, Liu Chongjie, lodged an informal protest with the German Propaganda Ministry, considering that Hitler's book "Mein Kampf" includes a chapter discussing "Blacks and Chinese" together, which made the Chinese feel embarrassed. This book, known as the bible of the National Socialist Party, has been published for many years and has been translated into Chinese. Ambassador Liu has also been in office for two years. It is not an appropriate time to raise the issue just before his departure, perhaps to fire a "parting shot".

However, our feelings are not like this. —

The racial fallacy was originally a pretext for imperialists to seize colonies. The National Socialist Party used it to shift the target of domestic people's struggle and strengthen Germany's reasons for demanding the restoration of the colonial empire. The political program of the National Socialist Party, the laws of its government (especially the recently promulgated anti-Jewish laws), and the speeches of Hitler, Goebbels, and other followers all prove that the National Socialist Party regards only the Aryan race as civilized people, and that Germans are the most excellent of the Aryan race. The so-called "Deutschland über Alles" has become a proud phrase in their party song. Since China, like Black Africa, has been a German colony, it is natural to discuss the "Blacks and Chinese" together because Chinese are also yellow-faced.

It is true that when China and Germany exchange ambassadors and try their best to get along with each other in other aspects, such a chapter is still retained in the famous works of the German leader, which has been reprinted countless times, which does indeed violate the purpose of friendly relations. No wonder that as soon as Ambassador Liu raised the issue, Mr. Fink, the acting Minister of Propaganda, "apologetically" agreed to cancel or revise it when the next edition is published. However, not to mention that "diplomatic rhetoric" and imperialist colonial policies can go hand in hand, even if this "bible" no longer contains anything that damages the dignity of the Chinese people in the future, will China's international status be enhanced from then on? Will the "Third Reich" no longer treat China as Black Africa, but desire to give it a try? This is still a big question.

It should be known that Germany, which emerged from defeat in the European War, has never forgotten China. Speaking of Qingdao, many Germans still have regrets and are salivating. Not to mention the National Socialist Party, which openly demands colonies. Although Sino-German relations are indeed friendly, Japanese-German relations are even more friendly. The widespread rumors in the newspapers about the secret German-Japanese agreement and the pro-Japanese arguments of the National Socialist Party's organ when Sino-Japanese disputes occurred prove what Germany's wooing of China is all about at heart.

If, because of the discussion of "Blacks and Chinese" together, it is pointed out as an insult, it is implying that oneself also recognizes Blacks as born inferior and should not be associated with the glorious Chinese nation with 5,000 years of culture. The current China, which calls for uniting the world's small and weak nations, does not seem to hold this racial fallacy with the taste of imperialists.

Page 22

Finally, in fact, the status of Chinese in foreign societies is not necessarily higher than that of Blacks. North America has special areas where Blacks gather, the ghetto, and San Francisco and London also have Chinatowns. Blacks are the source of ridicule and insult in American films. The pigtails and opium pipes of Chinamen are also malicious embellishments in American and even German Ufa films. Moreover, in the previous election in the United States, one of the presidential candidates was Black. Recently, Abyssinia, a Black country, desperately resisted the Italian invasion and did not accept the mediation plan of the imperialists, which is better than China. This is a fact that we all know and recognize. As a joke, some concession parks in China used to have signs saying "Dogs and Chinese are not allowed in," but in the eyes of some imperialists, Chinese are treated the same as dogs.

However, we are not saying that China should accept insults from imperialists submissively. On the contrary, China has many reasons to protest against discriminatory measures and remarks against Chinese by foreign countries. Not to mention the anti-Chinese laws in Nanyang and the Americas, even the fact that Hungary does not allow Chinese to enter the country and that Germany persecutes and even imprisons small businessmen from Qingtian, Zhejiang, should also be protested. As for greater oppression and aggression, it goes without saying that we should resist to the death like Abyssinia, a Black country.

The current protest, however, originates from the prejudice of being ashamed to be associated with Blacks, which not only exposes the spirit of Ah Q, but is also somewhat inappropriate in its wording.

Horse-drawn Carriage 223

— Lin Na

I arrived in Old Fuman Village around the New Year. The village was filled with revelry, and the carnival was about to begin. All of Manila was busy selecting the Carnival Queen. This village, like Manila, had a small street. Next door to us was a grocery store opened by an old councilor who had retired in 1925. The old councilor had gone blind and sat in the store all year round, leaning on a cane and loudly telling customers about his glorious past. The councilor's wife was still a middle-aged woman of about thirty-five or six, with two daughters in their late teens. These two modern sisters took out an old phonograph from the counter on Christmas Day and locked themselves in the house all day long, playing it loudly, singing and dancing wildly to the lewd songs, to the point that the whole village could hear.

The old councilor sat in his round chair, listening distractedly, his blind eyeballs covered with a white film twitching, a smile on his lips, tapping his cane lightly on the ground in time with the music. The councilor's wife also seemed very excited, darting nervously around the narrow store filled with cabinets, while the farmers, women, and children crowded outside the store, staring with their mouths open, listening distractedly. Several people who had run out of the wine shop, limping and stumbling, also hummed along in a low, hoarse voice, and danced in the street.

Finally, Songkui, the village police chief, also came. He slowly stepped down the street with a brisk pace. His neatly pressed yellow uniform shone slightly in the soft sunlight.

People busily made way for him, and he ran inside. He greeted the councilor's wife respectfully and asked the old councilor how he was. The old councilor trembled excitedly and shouted, "Old friend, it's been a long time! How have you been? Busy with work?" He pushed his cane away, stood up from the round chair, took a step forward, and opened his arms. Police Chief Songkui threw himself into his arms, and they hugged each other. After a while, the phonograph suddenly stopped. The two sisters heard it from the room and thought that a distinguished guest had arrived, so they opened the door half-naked. When they saw that it was Uncle Songkui, they looked displeased and ran back inside, pouting as if they were angry at someone. Finally, even the audience outside the store gradually dispersed, and the small street became quiet and solemn again.

The councilor's wife also took the time to go into the house, leaving the old councilor to watch the store. The old councilor smiled kindly and pulled the police chief close, asking, "Old friend, why haven't you been here lately? Really, God is my witness, I'm thinking of you all the time! I often think to myself and ask Rosa's mother, 'Why hasn't Uncle Songkui been here lately? Is it because we were slow to entertain him and he's angry?' She would say, 'Uncle Songkui is not that kind of person, he wouldn't blame us. He's probably busy with work and can't spare the time!' Really, old friend, you're too busy..."

"I'm not busy, but I've been running around lately for a robbery case..." Police Chief Songkui replied coldly.

"A robbery case? Which village again?" the old councilor asked in surprise, his blind eyes twitching nervously.

"It happened to a truck carrying goods from Manila in the Kepu forest area."

"So, any clues?"

"Several suspects have been arrested. Ke Tai from the village won't be able to escape!"

At this time, a heavy voice shouted loudly in the street. A heavily loaded carriage passed by, which excited the old councilor and reminded him of the Carnival that was raging in Manila. He inquired with Police Chief Songkui and sighed softly:

"Times have changed, alas! Uncle Songkui, when I think back to my time in the council, how excited we would be during such auspicious days! At that time, we had our own landau, the most respectable carriage you could find anywhere in Manila. On Christmas night, on the festive New Year's Eve, and even when the Carnival came, we would wear gorgeous clothes, and the Rosa sisters, when they were still young, would sit on either side of us. The coachman, Fu Jin, this little black fellow, sat solemnly on the driver's seat and turned around to ask, 'Sir, where to?' Then I would shout loudly, 'Isn't it the same as every year, to Manila, you blockhead!' Then he would turn around, whistling softly, the long whip flying in the air, and the horse would start walking. At this time, when we looked out of the car window, we often saw people crowded at the entrance of the village, watching us with envious eyes and waving their hands at us.

"But times have changed. The unfortunate have replaced the happy. Because of my unfortunate eyes, I was dismissed from my position as a councilor, and life has become more difficult day by day. First, we sold our villa on the Lunli Dai beach, and then even the chestnut mare and the landau were sold. At this time, I became so old! I will never see that respectable landau again, and Fu Jin's aggrieved face when he was scolded. The people who crowded at the entrance of the village watching us with envious eyes and waving their hands at us have also been replaced by new masters... Old friend, think about these lost days, how wonderful it is to think about them now!...

The old councilor said sadly. When Police Chief Songkui looked up, he also saw that the blind eyes of this unfortunate old friend were filled with teardrops the size of beans. (Manila Story, Part Two)

Chasing Rabbits 224

— Shi Dai

——A Small Scene in the Mountains and Fields of Qidong——

——Let's go! Let's chase rabbits! Let's chase rabbits!

Liu Shuangxi carried a large bundle of rabbit nets on his back, holding a lukewarm sweet potato in his right hand, eating as he walked. After swallowing a mouthful, he would take a moment to shout twice. When he reached Yu Qi's doorway, he stopped, threw away the sweet potato peel, and shouted again.

The snow had stopped long ago, and everyone had just finished breakfast. Some were mixing grass for the livestock in the pen, while others were squatting on the steps at the entrance smoking. The young people were overjoyed to hear someone calling to chase rabbits. They hurriedly put on their pigskin leggings, found their rabbit nets, grabbed a stick from the courtyard, and ran into the street.

In a short while, many people gathered at Yu Qi's doorway, carrying nets and pulling sticks.

They followed the willow trees along the riverbank at the edge of the village, diagonally crossing the frozen river, heading towards Tianzi Ridge. The distant mountains were covered in dazzling white, the fields were dazzling white, and the diagonal valleys were dazzling white. Everyone was talking, laughing, arguing, and making noise, like a swarm of flies landing on white granulated sugar, buzzing incessantly. The snow crunched under their feet, and the tobacco in their pipes mixed with their exhaled breath, slowly disappearing into the cold.

Passing through the deep valley, the pine forest appeared before them. The snow pressed down on the pine branches, and the half-dead pine needles quietly hid under the branches, looking up at the snow blossoms above. The smooth, bare oak trees had branches that seemed to be wrapped in a layer of soft cotton. There was no storm, no dark clouds, and the sunlight fell on the snow, reflecting a glistening shine.

When they reached the foot of Tianzi Ridge, they stopped.

Everyone argued and yielded in disorder. Some said they should set up the nets here, while others said this place was not as good as the slope on the east side. They argued back and forth for a long time. Then Yu Qi spoke up, saying that according to his experience, this was an excellent place. No one insisted, so they began to set up the nets. Liu Shuangxi and Xiao Shunzi hid under the short pine branches at the end of the net, stabilizing their bodies. The rest of the people pulled their sticks and ran off in all directions, the mountain filled with shouts. Sticks beat against the pine trees, and the peaceful snow was trampled on.

The rabbit is the most alert and timid of animals. It silently hides under a small bush close to the ground, shrinking its body and fighting the cold. When it hears human voices shouting, it runs off in a panic. It runs east and encounters shouts, then turns back and runs west, but the shouts are just as loud there. It then cleverly runs in the direction where there are no shouts. Suddenly, the sound waves behind it rise higher, chasing after it. It uses its last bit of strength and runs forward recklessly. Just when it thinks it has escaped with its life, it runs into the net and is held down by someone.

——Nine in total!—— Yu Qi happily tied the rabbit's hind legs together, a clear drip of snot hanging from his nose.

Then everyone gathered again, packing up the nets, tying the straps, smoking, blowing their noses, and coughing. When they put the nets on their shoulders, someone suggested going to Huangniu Mountain for another round. But everyone was already tired, and no one wanted to expend their last bit of energy under this cold, fierce assault.

The crowd wriggled across the snow, passed through the pine forest, and crossed the deep valley. Talking and laughing made them forget their fatigue.

On the way home, the sun pointed directly south, and the smoke from the village chimneys appeared in a deep gray color in the cold air. Hunger stirred in the crowd.

Anniversary of Death 225

— Si Quan

On the anniversary of my maternal uncle's death, I arrived from the station with a sorrowful heart and took a car directly to my uncle's house. My uncle's family used to be a prominent clan in the county. Although it was not as prosperous as before during my uncle's time, the large five-courtyard residence still stood proudly, and the Protector Village Bridge was always renovated to look new. The car stopped by the Protector Village River, and I could see the white paper streamers on the two door panels fluttering in the cold wind from afar. I strolled across the Protector Village Bridge. The path in front of the village was covered with newly fallen dead leaves, as if no one had walked here this morning. Approaching the gate, the door panels were ajar. I walked straight into the third courtyard, which was the main hall. The elegiac couplets and banners hanging on the four walls were faded. I stood there blankly, thinking of my uncle's life. In just one year, everything had died with my uncle's death! Entering the side courtyard, the old maid cried out as if she had found a treasure, "Young nephew is here!"

She told me that my aunt was bedridden upstairs and had not gotten up for two months. The young master didn't care about anything and stretched out his hand to ask his mother for money every day. The old maid shed two clear tears and led me upstairs. My aunt seemed to have heard my voice long ago, propped herself up halfway, and waited for me. She beckoned me to sit in front of her bed, and like when I was a child, she reached out to touch my cheek as soon as she saw me, and said in a trembling voice, "You still remember your uncle's anniversary."

I had learned some things about my uncle's family over the past year from people from my hometown. My uncle liked to do good deeds during his lifetime, and the loans he made to others were all without contracts. But when he had financial difficulties, he would rather take out loans. After my uncle died, my aunt sold the fields to repay them. As for the money loaned to others, it naturally disappeared without a trace. My cousin was also unproductive, but contrary to expectations, my uncle's family did not fall to such a miserable state. On the anniversary of my uncle's death, not a single relative or friend came to mourn! I lowered my head, not daring to look directly at my aunt. I secretly looked at her thin wrist. I regretted making this trip, because my coming from afar might have made my aunt even more sad!

The old maid was an old servant in my uncle's family. Perhaps she also had a bellyful of grievances to tell me, and she often cast glances at me; but my aunt, the mistress, did not speak. After a while, she said, "Young nephew, talk to the mistress, I'll go downstairs to brew tea."

My aunt then sighed.

"Thanks to her, I didn't die of illness! I don't know what sins I committed to leave behind this treasure. Your uncle did good deeds all his life, only to end up like this. What else is there to say!" My aunt seemed a little more excited and reached out her trembling hand again to stroke my hair. "You don't know yet, do you? After your uncle died, people came to the door to collect debts almost every day. I never participated in the income and expenditure of money. Your uncle was frugal, and until his death, he pretended not to be sick, because he couldn't bear to call a doctor! Look, after he died, what did it become! That treasure only knows how to reach out his hand for money. I've been sick for more than two months, and he doesn't know to call a doctor. When he comes to my room, it's only to ask for money. It's not like before now, and people are so bad. Where did your uncle mistreat people? Not a single soul came to the door on his first anniversary. Just think, this family's fortune was not easily earned!"

My aunt's voice rose higher and higher. The grievances accumulated in her heart seemed to be vented in this opportunity, and the hand stroking my hair tightened, as if she wanted to grab something to vent her anger. I held back my tears,
